In particular, bitcoin mining companies, which are essential to the currency's underlying technology, are flashing warning signs."<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[137]</a></sup> Also in January 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Dark_web" title="Dark web">deep web</a> drug dealers were "freaking out" as they lost profits through being unable to convert bitcoin revenue to cash quickly enough as the price declined – and that there was a danger that dealers selling reserves to stay in business might force the bitcoin price down further.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[138]</a></sup></p> 
         <p>According to an article in <i>The Wall Street Journal</i>, as of 19 April 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, bitcoin had been more stable than gold for the preceding 24 days, and it was suggested that its value might be more stable in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[139]</a></sup> On 3 March 2017, the price of a bitcoin surpassed the market value of an ounce of <a href="/wiki/Gold_as_an_investment" title="Gold as an investment">gold</a> for the first time as its price surged to an all-time high.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[141]</a></sup> A study in <i>Electronic Commerce Research and Applications</i>, going back through the network's historical data, showed the value of the bitcoin network as measured by the price of bitcoins, to be roughly proportional to the square of the number of daily unique users participating on the network. This is a form of <a href="/wiki/Metcalfe%27s_law" title="Metcalfe's law">Metcalfe's law</a> and suggests that the network was demonstrating network effects proportional to its level of user adoption.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[142]</a></sup></p> 
         <h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Ponzi_scheme_concerns">Ponzi scheme concerns</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Ponzi scheme concerns" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h3> 
         <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
          See also: 
          <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_bitcoin#Ponzi_scheme_concerns" title="Economics of bitcoin">Economics of bitcoin §&nbsp;Ponzi scheme concerns</a>
         </div> 
         <p>Various journalists,<sup id="cite_ref-dh150613_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dh150613-67">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[143]</a></sup> economists,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dd_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dd-154">[145]</a></sup> and the central bank of Estonia<sup id="cite_ref-Ott_Ummelas_and_Milda_Seputyte_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ott_Ummelas_and_Milda_Seputyte-155">[146]</a></sup> have voiced concerns that bitcoin is a <a href="/wiki/Ponzi_scheme" title="Ponzi scheme">Ponzi scheme</a>. <a href="/wiki/Eric_Posner" title="Eric Posner">Eric Posner</a>, a law professor at the University of Chicago, stated in 2013 that "a real Ponzi scheme takes fraud; bitcoin, by contrast, seems more like a collective delusion."<sup id="cite_ref-Posner.2C_Eric_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Posner.2C_Eric-156">[147]</a></sup> In 2014 reports by both the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:7</sup> and the Swiss <a href="/wiki/Federal_Council_(Switzerland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Council (Switzerland)">Federal Council</a><sup id="cite_ref-FC20140625_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FC20140625-158">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:21</sup> examined the concerns and came to the conclusion that bitcoin is not a Ponzi scheme. In 2017 billionaire <a href="/wiki/Howard_Marks_(investor)" title="Howard Marks (investor)">Howard Marks</a> referred to bitcoin as a pyramid scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[150]</a></sup></p> 
         <p>On September 12, 2017 <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Dimon" title="Jamie Dimon">Jamie Dimon</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/JP_Morgan_Chase" class="mw-redirect" title="JP Morgan Chase">JP Morgan Chase</a>, called bitcoin a "fraud" and said he would fire anyone in his firm caught trading it. <a href="/wiki/Zero_Hedge" title="Zero Hedge">Zero Hedge</a> claimed that the same day Dimon made his statement, JP Morgan also purchased a large amount of bitcoins for its clients.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[151]</a></sup> On September 13th, 2017 Dimon followed up and compared bitcoin to a bubble, saying it was only useful for drug dealers and countries like North Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[152]</a></sup> On 22 September 2017, hedge fund Blockswater subsequently accused JP Morgan of market manipulation and filed a market abuse complaint with <a href="/wiki/Financial_Supervisory_Authority_(Sweden)" title="Financial Supervisory Authority (Sweden)">Swedish Financial Supervisory Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[153]</a></sup></p> 
        </div>
        <h2 class="in-block section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)">
         <div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator"></div><span id="Legal_status,_tax_and_regulation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status.2C_tax_and_regulation">Legal status, tax and regulation</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Legal status, tax and regulation" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h2>
        <div class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5"> 
         <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
          Main article: 
          <a href="/wiki/Legality_of_bitcoin_by_country_or_territory" title="Legality of bitcoin by country or territory">Legality of bitcoin by country or territory</a>
         </div> 
         <p>Because of bitcoin's decentralized nature, restrictions or bans on its use are impossible to enforce, although it can be criminalized.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[154]</a></sup> The legal status of bitcoin varies substantially from country to country and is still undefined or changing in many of them. While some countries have explicitly allowed its use and trade, others have banned or restricted it. Regulations and bans that apply to bitcoin probably extend to similar cryptocurrency systems.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[155]</a></sup></p> 
        </div>
        <h2 class="in-block section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)">
         <div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_activity">Criminal activity</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Criminal activity" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h2>
        <div class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6"> 
         <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
          See also: 
          <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_network#Criminal_activity" title="Bitcoin network">Bitcoin network §&nbsp;Criminal activity</a>
         </div> 
         <p>The use of bitcoin by criminals has attracted the attention of financial regulators, legislative bodies, law enforcement, and the media.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavin.2C_Tim_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavin.2C_Tim-165">[156]</a></sup> The FBI prepared an intelligence assessment,<sup id="cite_ref-fbi_report_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbi_report-166">[157]</a></sup> the SEC has issued a pointed warning about investment schemes using virtual currencies,<sup id="cite_ref-Lavin.2C_Tim_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavin.2C_Tim-165">[156]</a></sup> and the U.S. Senate held a hearing on virtual currencies in November 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-USoff_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USoff-66">[59]</a></sup></p> 
         <p>Several news outlets have asserted that the popularity of bitcoins hinges on the ability to use them to purchase illegal goods.<sup id="cite_ref-Monetarists_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monetarists-101">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[158]</a></sup> In 2014, researchers at the University of Kentucky found "robust evidence that computer programming enthusiasts and illegal activity drive interest in bitcoin, and find limited or no support for political and investment motives."<sup id="cite_ref-uok_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uok-168">[159]</a></sup></p> 
        </div>
        <h2 class="in-block section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)">
         <div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="In_academia">In academia</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: In academia" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h2>
        <div class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7"> 
         <h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Journals">Journals</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Journals" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h3> 
         <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
          Main article: 
          <a href="/wiki/Ledger_(journal)" title="Ledger (journal)">Ledger (journal)</a>
         </div> 
         <p>In September 2015, the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Peer-reviewed" class="mw-redirect" title="Peer-reviewed">peer-reviewed</a> <a href="/wiki/Academic_journal" title="Academic journal">academic journal</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Ledger_(journal)" title="Ledger (journal)">Ledger</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="International Standard Serial Number (identifier)">ISSN</a>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/search?fq=x0:jrnl&amp;q=n2:2379-5980">2379-5980</a>) was announced. It will cover studies of cryptocurrencies and related technologies, and is published by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[161]</a></sup> The journal encourages authors to <a href="/wiki/Digital_signature" title="Digital signature">digitally sign</a> a <a href="/wiki/Hash_function" title="Hash function">file hash</a> of submitted papers, which will then be <a href="/wiki/Trusted_timestamping" title="Trusted timestamping">timestamped</a> into the bitcoin <a href="/wiki/Blockchain_(database)" class="mw-redirect" title="Blockchain (database)">blockchain</a>. Authors are also asked to include a personal bitcoin address in the first page of their papers.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[163]</a></sup></p> 
         <h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Other" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h3> 
         <p>In the fall of 2014, undergraduate students at the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> (MIT) each received bitcoins worth $100 "to better understand this emerging technology". The bitcoins were not provided by MIT but rather the MIT Bitcoin Club, a student-run club.<sup id="cite_ref-MIT_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIT-173">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[165]</a></sup></p> 
         <p>In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> launched a lab course on building bitcoin-enabled applications.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[166]</a></sup></p> 
        </div>
        <h2 class="in-block section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)">
         <div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator"></div><span id="In_art,_entertainment,_and_media"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="In_art.2C_entertainment.2C_and_media">In art, entertainment, and media</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: In art, entertainment, and media" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h2>
        <div class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8"> 
         <h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Films">Films</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Films" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h3> 
         <p>The documentary film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rise_and_Rise_of_Bitcoin" title="The Rise and Rise of Bitcoin">The Rise and Rise of Bitcoin</a></i> (late 2014), features interviews with people who use bitcoin, such as a computer programmer and a drug dealer.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[167]</a></sup></p> 
         <h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Music" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h3> 
         <p>Several lighthearted songs celebrating bitcoin have been released.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[168]</a></sup></p> 
         <h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Literature" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h3> 
         <p>In <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stross" title="Charles Stross">Charles Stross</a>' science fiction novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Neptune%27s_Brood" title="Neptune's Brood">Neptune's Brood</a></i> (2013), a modification of bitcoin is used as the universal <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_travel" title="Interstellar travel">interstellar</a> payment system.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[169]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="The claim is a conclusion based on a primary source (July 2017)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
        </div>
        <h2 class="in-block section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)">

        <h2 class="in-block section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)">
         <div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notes" data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-edit-enabled edit-page">Edit</a></span></h2>
        <div class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10"> 
         <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;"> 
          <ol class="references">
           <li id="cite_note-BTCcode-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-BTCcode_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BTCcode_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, BTC is a commonly used code.<sup id="cite_ref-standardize_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-standardize-3">[2]</a></sup> It does not conform to <a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">ISO 4217</a> as BT is the country code of Bhutan, and ISO 4217 requires the first letter used in global commodities to be 'X'.</span></li> 
           <li id="cite_note-XBTcode-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-XBTcode_8-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-XBTcode_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, XBT, a code that conforms to ISO 4217 though is not officially part of it, is used by <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg L.P.</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CNNMoney" title="CNNMoney">CNNMoney</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[4]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Xe.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Xe.com">xe.com</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[5]</a></sup></span></li> 
           <li id="cite_note-BTCsym-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-BTCsym_10-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BTCsym_10-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The symbol was encoded in <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> version 10.0 at position U+20BF (?) in the <a href="/wiki/Currency_Symbols_(Unicode_block)" title="Currency Symbols (Unicode block)">Currency Symbols block</a> in June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-unicode-10_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicode-10-9">[6]</a></sup></span></li> 
           <li id="cite_note-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-37">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Relative mining difficulty is defined as the ratio of the difficulty target on 9 January 2009 to the current difficulty target.</span></li> 
           <li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is misleading to think that there is an analogy between gold mining and bitcoin mining. The fact is that gold miners are rewarded for producing gold, while bitcoin miners are not rewarded for producing bitcoins; they are rewarded for their record-keeping services.<sup id="cite_ref-Andolfatto2014-03_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andolfatto2014-03-38">[33]</a></sup></span></li> 
           <li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The exact number is 20,999,999.9769 bitcoins.<sup id="cite_ref-Antonopoulos2014_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-11">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:ch. 8</sup></span></li> 
           <li id="cite_note-135"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-135">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The price of 1 bitcoin in U.S. dollars.</span></li> 
           <li id="cite_note-136"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-136">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Volatility is calculated on a yearly basis.</span></li> 
          </ol>
         </div> 
        </div>
